regular planning and zoning commission meeting the preliminary plat shall be reviewed in general and if acceptable shall be referred by the planning and zoning commission to the following offices for study a city engineers office  b electric company  c gas company  d telephone company  e cable television company  f all other franchised utility companies doing business in the city  and g cities located within five miles of the area to be subdivided the school district and where applicable special utility districts and the state department of transportation 2 each of these offices shall return its recommendation to the planning and zoning commission within 30 days of receipt of its copy of the preliminary plat 3 failure to respond within this comment period will be interpreted as no objection and the city shall have no further responsibility for plat review coordination with nonresponding offices 4 at the following regular planning and zoning commission meeting and after discussion with the subdivider on changes deemed advisable including the kind and extent of improvements to be made by him or her the planning and zoning commission shall disapprove approve as submitted or approve as modified the preliminary plat 5 action by the planning and zoning commission shall be conveyed to the subdivider in writing within ten days after the official planning and zoning commission meeting at which the plat was considered in case the plat is disapproved the subdivider shall be notified of the reason for such action and what requirements shall be necessary to meet the approval of the planning and zoning commission the approval of the preliminary plat does not constitute an acceptance of the subdivision but is deemed to be an authorization to proceed with the preparation of the final plat the approval of the preliminary plat shall only be effective for a period of one year unless an extension is granted by the planning and zoning commission if the final plat has not been submitted for approval within the specified period a preliminary plat must be submitted again to the planning and zoning commission for approval   art iii 1986   1997   2000 final plat a submission 1 after approval of the preliminary plat the subdivider shall submit a final plat for recording purposes to the secretary of the planning and zoning commission such plat shall be accompanied by the required filing fee a sample plat is available in the planning department 2 the original on mylar tracing cloth or similar material and ten prints thereof shall be submitted to the secretary of the planning and zoning commission at least ten days prior to the planning and zoning commission public hearing 3 the names and signatures of the owner or of the property duly acknowledged and notarized shall appear on the original copies submitted 4 the final plat prepared for recording purposes shall be drawn at a scale of at least one inch equals 100 feet or larger the size of the sheet on which such final plat is prepared shall be 22 inches by 36 inches b information the final plat shall incorporate any required modifications of the preliminary plat and shall show and contain the following information 1 name of subdivision which shall not duplicate or too closely approximate the name of any existing subdivision  2 location of section township range county and state including the descriptive boundaries of the subdivision based on an accurate traverse giving angular and linear dimensions which must be mathematically close the allowable error of closing on any portion of the plat shall be one foot in 5000 feet  3 the locations of monuments shall be shown and described on the final plat locations of such monuments shall be shown in reference to existing official monuments or the nearest established street lines including the true angles and distances to such reference points or monuments  4 the locations of lots streets public highways alleys parks and other features with accurate dimensions in feet and decimals of feet and with the length of radii on all curves and other information necessary to reproduce the plat on the ground dimensions from all curves shall be shown to the lot lines  5 be numbered clearly blocks shall be numbered or lettered clearly in the center of the block all lots however designated shall be numbered in progressive numbers or by blocks in which they are situated and their precise lengths and widths shall be stated on the map or plat  6 the exact locations widths and names of all streets to be dedicated  7 locations and widths of all easements and alleys to be dedicated  8 boundary lines and descriptions of the boundary lines of any area other than streets and alleys which are to be dedicated or reserved for public use  9 building setback lines on the front and side streets with dimensions  10 names and addresses of the developer and the registered professional engineer who prepared the plat  11 scale of the plat scale is to be shown graphically and in feet per inch date of preparation and north point  12 statement dedicating all easements  13 statement dedicating all streets alleys and all other public areas not previously dedicated  and 14 mailing address of the property after subdivision c final plat review 1 at the next regular planning and zoning commission meeting the planning and zoning commission shall check the final plat for conformity with the approved preliminary plat and other requirements of this chapter and shall then approve or disapprove the final plat as submitted 2 as a condition to the approval of a final plat the subdivider or landowner shall agree to install improvements as noted and specified in article iii of this chapter d recording 1 not more than three months after approval of the final plat by the planning and zoning commission the subdivider shall record the final plat in the manner and condition prescribed in section 2269 after three months the approving action of the planning and zoning commission shall be deemed to have been withdrawn 2 also required is a final survey of utilities as installed to be submitted to the city engineer it can be a simplified version of the engineering drawings but it should record the necessary minor changes of location that are always made in the course of construction certificates of improvements completion will be withheld until this survey is made   art iii 1986   2000 secs 2272230  reserved article ii  design standards blocks a design the lengths widths and shapes of blocks shall be determined with due regard to 1 provision of adequate building sites suitable to the special needs of the type of use contemplated  2 zoning requirements as to lot sizes and dimensions  3 needs for convenient access circulation control and safety of street traffic  and 4 limitations and opportunities of topography b length intersecting streets which determine block lengths shall be provided at such intervals as to serve crosstraffic adequately and to meet existing streets in the neighborhood in residential districts where no existing plats are recorded the blocks shall not exceed 750 feet in length except that in outlying subdivisions a greater length may be permitted where topography or other conditions justify a departure from this maximum in blocks longer than 600 feet pedestrian ways andor easements block may be required by the planning and zoning commission near the center of the block such pedestrian ways or easements shall have a minimum width of ten feet blocks for business use should normally not exceed 600 feet in length c width in residential subdivisions the block width shall normally be sufficient to allow two tiers of lots of appropriate depth blocks intended for business or industrial use shall be of such width and depth as may be considered most suitable for the prospective use   art iii 1986   2000 streets alleys and public ways a the arrangement of streets in new subdivisions shall make provisions for the continuation of the principal existing streets in adjoining additions or their proper projection where adjoining property is not subdivided insofar as they may be necessary for public requirements 1 the width of such streets in new subdivisions shall not be less than the minimum street widths established herein 2 alleys when required and street arrangement must also be such as not to cause hardship to owners of adjoining property when they plat their land and seek to provide for convenient access to it 3 whenever there exists a dedicated or platted halfstreet or alley adjacent to the tract to be subdivided the other half of the street or alley shall be platted and dedicated as a public way b streets that are obviously in alignment with other already existing named streets shall bear the names of the existing streets c major streets shall conform with the major street plan as adopted by the planning and zoning commission and the governing body d minor streets shall be so designed as to discourage nonlocal traffic e culdesacs or deadend streets shall be permitted only when topography or ownership prevents normal subdivision of a tract or plot of ground said culdesacs shall normally be no longer than 500 feet including a turnaround at the closed end having an outside roadway diameter of at least 100 feet with a street property line diameter of at least 110 feet f under normal conditions streets shall be laid out to intersect as nearly as possible at right angles where topography or other conditions justify a variation from the right angle intersection the minimum angle shall be 60 degrees g where lots front or side but do not back on railroad rightsofway limited access freeways or principal highways a marginal access street or frontage road shall be provided parallel and adjacent to the boundary of such rightofway the distance of the street from said rightofway shall be determined with due consideration given to minimum distance required for approach connections to future grade separations h dedication of halfstreets will not be approved except where it is essential to the reasonable development of the subdivision and is in conformity with the approved major street plan and other requirements of this chapter i alleys shall be provided in commercial and industrial districts except that the requirements may be waived where other definite and ensured provisions are made for service access to offstreet loading and unloading areas and to offstreet parking areas consistent with and adequate for the uses proposed deadend alleys shall be avoided wherever possible but if unavoidable adequate turnaround facilities shall be provided alleys may be required in certain residential areas   art iv 1986   2000 minimum requirements all streets alleys and public ways included in any subdivision hereafter dedicated and accepted shall not be less than the minimum dimensions for each classification as follows classification width major streets arterial 80 feet collector 70 feet local street 60 feet culdesac 50foot radius on turnaround marginal access streets or frontage roads oneway 50 feet twoway 60 feet alley 20 feet pedestrian way 10 feet   art iv 1986 additional requirements a when existing or anticipated traffic on arterial and collector thoroughfares warrants greater widths of rightsofway the additional width shall be provided b drainage easements shall be required in addition to street rightsofway where the streets adjoin or are parallel with streams or drainage areas or where lots back on said drainage areas the width of such drainage easement shall be determined by the city engineer who shall notify the planning and zoning commission of his or her recommendation in writing c the grades of streets alleys and other public ways included in any subdivision shall not be greater than is necessary for the topographical conditions d minimum horizontal and vertical alignment on all streets except in unusual cases shall be as follows 1 horizontal alignment radii at the centerline a major streets 300 feet b local streets 100 feet a tangent shall be provided between all reversed curves to provide for a smooth flow of traffic 2 vertical alignment all changes in street grade shall be connected by vertical curves of such length as to provide for the desired sight distance   art iv 1986   2000 a the minimum lot width shall be 50 feet except where additional width is required on corner lots to maintain a front yard on both streets said width shall be measured at the building setback line b the minimum lot depth shall be 120 feet except where additional depth is required on corner lots said measurement shall be measured center of the lot and shall be perpendicular to the property line or radial to the property line on curved streets c minimum area shall be subject to the zoning regulations of the district in which the subdivision is located d subdivisions to be served with an approved public water system but not with an approved public sanitary sewer system shall be sized according to soil percolation tests made by a registered professional engineer such tests shall be made in accordance with state department of health criteria in no case shall any such lot contain less than onehalf acre and all lots shall be so proportioned as to permit future replotting consistent with good subdivision design e subdivisions to be served with an approved public sanitary sewer system but not with an approved public water system shall contain not less than onehalf acre unless otherwise approved by the planning and zoning commission all lots shall be so proportioned that future replatting will be consistent with good subdivision design f subdivisions not served by either an approved public sewer system or an approved public water system shall be sized on the basis of soil percolation tests made by a registered professional engineer such tests shall be in accordance with state department of health criteria in no case shall such lots be less than 212 acres in area and all lots shall be so proportioned as to permit future replatting consistent with good subdivision design g all side lot lines shall bear 60 degrees to 90 degrees from the street rightofway line on a straight street or from the tangent of a curved street h corner lots in residential subdivisions shall have additional width in order that the same setback on both streets may be observed i double frontage lots shall be avoided unless in the opinion of the planning and zoning commission a variation to this rule will give better street alignment and lot arrangement j every lot shall abut on a street other than an alley k building or setback lines shall be shown on the preliminary and final plats for all lots in the subdivision and shall not be less than the setback required by chapter 30 l the subdivision or resubdivision of a tract or lot shall not be permitted where said subdivision or resubdivision places an existing permanent structure in violation of the requirements of chapter 30   art iv 1986   2000 easements a where alleys are not provided permanent easements of not less than 712 feet in width shall be provided on each side of all rear lot lines and on side lot lines where necessary for utility poles wires and conduits  sanitary sewers  gas water and heat mains  and other public utilities these easements shall provide for a continuous rightofway at least 15 feet in width b a 12foot temporary construction easement shall be provided on each side of the permanent easement required in subsection a of this section for initial construction of water sewer and other utility lines c where a subdivision is traversed by or is adjacent to a watercourse drainage way channel or stream there shall be provided a stormwater easement or drainage rightofway conforming substantially with the lines of such watercourse and such further width as may be required for the construction of necessary flood control measures   art iv 1986 dedication or reservation of public sites and open spaces in all subdivisions consideration shall be given to potential needs for sites for schools parks playgrounds or other public use areas and open spaces any such dedication or reservation shall conform as nearly as possible to the recommendations of the planning and zoning commission with regard to the intent of the comprehensive plan and to the recommendations of other public agencies to be involved all areas to be dedicated or reserved for public use shall be shown on the preliminary plat in order that it may be determined when and in what manner such areas will be dedicated to or acquired by the appropriate agency   art v 1986   2000 secs 22382262  reserved article iii  improvements generally a the subdivider shall cause to be installed and constructed all street and road improvements public utilities survey monuments and markers and lot grading all such improvements shall conform to the requirements of this chapter and all other applicable county and state standards specifications codes and regulations these standards may be obtained among others from the city clerk county clerk planning and zoning commission state department of transportation and state department of health general guidelines for such improvements include the following 1 streets shall be surfaced with concrete asphaltic concrete or materials and specifications in accordance with the city requirements and shall include curb and storm sewer inlets where applicable 2 where an approved public water system is proposed to serve the subdivision said water lines shall be installed in proper easements or within the limits of the street and alley rightofway and shall be of a size as approved by the city council 3 where an approved public sewer system is proposed to serve the subdivision the sewer system shall be constructed to provide service to each lot within the subdivision the system of mains and laterals shall collect the sewage within the subdivision and discharge it into a community disposal system approved by the city council 4 street signs will be supplied and erected by the city council 5 installation of electric service power lines transformers and street lights shall be provided and paid for in accordance with policies established by the utilities board 6 sidewalks shall be installed on both sides of all streets and shall have a minimum width of five feet unless otherwise approved by the city council b if other improvements are required such as tree planting retaining walls drainage structures etc such improvements shall be made in accordance with the recommendations and specifications of the city council   art vi 1986   2000 financing of required improvements a the subdivider shall be responsible for the cost of required improvements which include the following 1 setting of survey monuments and markers  2 street and road construction for all minor street improvements including base grading curbs gutters sidewalks pavement street trees street name signs culverts and bridges  3 water and sewer line installations including fire hydrants and manholes  4 required storm sewer system andor other drainage improvements  5 lot grading and site preparation  6 landscaping and fencing where this is made a provision of any approval  and 7 any other site improvement made a requirement for development by the planning and zoning commission or city council b the subdivider shall also be responsible for ensuring the installation of the following by negotiating with public agencies or private companies or by providing the cash for their installation 1 electric lines  2 telephone lines  3 street lights  4 natural gas lines where required by the planning and zoning commission  5 street name signs  6 cable television service lines  and 7 permanent survey monuments at locations approved by the planning and zoning commission in conjunction with the city engineer provided that ordinarily such monuments shall not be more than 1320 feet nor less than 660 feet apart  and in addition monuments of iron pipe stone or concrete shall be set at all street intersections at all tangent points at alley intersections at all lot corners and at such other points as may be required by the planning and zoning commission to make the retracing of the lines shown on the final plat reasonably convenient c in the event that improvements are required by the planning and zoning commission that are oversized for the improvement capacity required for the subdivision the city county state or responsible district shall pay for improvement installation costs that are in excess of those necessary to meet the requirements of the subdivision these may include among others the following 1 street improvements in excess of those for minor or local streets but not including rightsofway  2 trunk sewer and water lines but not including easements  and 3 storm sewers of a size larger than required for proper drainage of the subdivision d the city may assess a subdivider on a pro rata basis for costs of improvements that have been made that benefit the subdivider or subdivision that would have been necessary costs to the subdivider had they not previously been expended such expenditures may have been made by either a governmental agency or by a private individual with a governmental agency such improvements may include among others the following 1 street improvements abutting unsubdivided land  or 2 sewer or water line installations that will serve unsubdivided land when subdivided any monies so collected shall be refunded to the agency or individual who made the original investment e the subdivider shall submit an estimate of the costs of constructing the required improvements to determine the amount of performance guarantee to be required the estimate shall specify the sources used as a basis to determine unit and project costs the planning and zoning commission shall make any checks and revisions in the estimates as they deem necessary prior to approval at the request of the subdivider the planning and zoning commission shall hold a noticepublished public hearing prior to making any and all revisions in the subdividers cost estimate the cost of publishing notice of the hearing shall be borne by the subdivider   art vi 1986   2000 engineering drawings a the planning and zoning commission in conjunction with the city engineer and other appropriate public agencies shall approve all engineering drawings and construction plans prior to the commencement of any work by the subdivider all required supplementary engineering studies or tests as required by the planning and zoning commission shall be approved prior to any construction activities by or for the subdivider b all required engineering studies and exhibits shall be prepared by qualified and legally registered or certified engineers or engineering firms c contractors engaged by the subdivider to install required improvements shall be licensed registered or certified as required by state or local law d a time construction schedule of installation of public improvements shall be submitted to and approved by the planning and zoning commission prior to the commencement of any and all construction activities the approved schedule shall be flexible enough to allow delays due to inclement weather or other unavoidable circumstances in the event that construction at some time can no longer adhere to the approved schedule the subdivider shall submit a revised schedule to the planning and zoning commission for approval e it may be desirable during construction of improvements for the subdivider to modify some standards and specifications of the approved engineering drawings in this event the subdivider shall prior to making such modifications submit a schedule of such modifications with reasons of necessity to the planning and zoning commission for approval f in the event that any modifications as specified in subsection e of this section are approved by the planning and zoning commission the subdivider shall submit asbuilt drawings   art vi 1986   2000 guarantees of performance a before acceptance of a plat by the planning and zoning commission the subdivider shall have designated all necessary streets and alleys in the proposed subdivision together with sidewalks curbs and gutters in accordance with the requirements that the planning and zoning commission may impose and specify as to grading paving width location drainage courts culverts bridges and other necessary requirements the subdivider shall enter into a written agreement with the planning and zoning commission wherein the subdivider shall have deposited a performance bond in an amount established by the planning and zoning commission or have deposited with the city sufficient funds to cover the cost of such improvements or provide other improvement guarantees acceptable to the planning and zoning commission and the city council which shall be recorded in the office of the county clerk the amount of the performance bond or the funds in escrow shall be determined from the cost estimates as specified in this article b the planning and zoning commission shall also require a maintenance bond to remain in effect for one year after acceptance of said improvements to be posted by the subdivider to ensure the repairs to any installations after completion and acceptance by the city that are made necessary due to negligence whether intentional or accidental by the subdivider such required repairs might include among others the following 1 damage to streets and highways caused by transporting heavy construction equipment over them  or 2 cutting and breaking street improvements to provide additional utility connections   art vi 1986   2000 inspection of improvements a the subdivider shall obtain construction permits for any construction work when required by state or local law b inspection schedules as required by state or local law shall be adhered to by the subdivider the subdivider shall notify the appropriate governmental agency as required by law when certain stages of construction have been reached the responsible governmental agency shall within 24 working hours inspect the indicated construction and notify the subdivider of its acceptability or unacceptability if for some reason an improvement is unacceptable the inspector shall indicate to the subdivider by reference to an unmet legal requirement what steps shall be taken by the subdivider to make the improvement acceptable   art vi 1986   2000 variances for hardship whenever it is found that the land included in a subdivision plat presented for approval is of such size or shape is subject to or is affected by such topographical location or conditions or is to be devoted to such usage that full conformity to the provisions of this chapter is impossible or is impractical the planning and zoning commission may recommend to the city council by letter that the city council authorize a variance or exception in the final plat so that substantial justice may be done and the public interest secured in recommending such variance or exception the planning and zoning commission shall find the following 1 that there are special circumstances or conditions affecting the property  2 that the variance or exception is necessary for the reasonable and acceptable development of the property in question  and 3 that the granting of the variance or exception will not be detrimental to the public welfare or injurious to adjacent property   art vii 1986   2000 miscellaneous a building and zoning permits no building permit or zoning permit shall be issued for any structure that is located upon a lot in an area that has not been subdivided unless the subdivision of said lands has been approved according to the requirements in effect at the time of subdivision b recording no plat replat dedication or deed of a street or public way shall be filed with the register of deeds until such plat replat dedication or deed shall have endorsed on it the fact that it has been submitted and approved by the planning and zoning commission and by the city council pursuant to the standards and procedures provided in for in this in this article shall require the acceptance of any dedication or deed by the city council c certifications required on final plat when the final plat is approved certifications shall be made on the final plat signed and acknowledged by all parties holding title or having any title interest in the land subdivided and consenting to the preparation and recording of the plat as submitted the original and ten copies of the plat submitted shall carry the signatures of the owners and shall be duly notarized by a notary public d a registered professional engineer shall sign and place his or her seal on the final plat certifying that the physical and mathematical details on the plat are correct e certification of the official approval of the final plat shall provide for date and signature of the following 1 chairperson and secretary of the planning and zoning commission  2 city council to be signed by the mayor and attested by the city clerk  3 entry for the date and transfer of record with space for the signature of the county clerk  and 4 space for the recording of the instrument and the name of the register of deeds   art viii 1986   2000 supplemental documents to accompany the final plat a two prints of profiles of streets to be dedicated commission such final plat together with the recommendation of the planning and zoning commission shall be transmitted to the city council for its review and action b upon receipt of any approved final plat from the planning and zoning commission and its recommendation thereon the city council shall schedule a public hearing upon said final plat and planning and zoning commission recommendation notice of such public hearing shall be given by posting of the premises proposed to be subdivided and by publication in the manner of other legal publications at least ten days prior to the date of such public hearing following public hearing the city council in its discretion may approve approve as modified or disapprove any such final plat submitted   art viii 1986   1997   2000 and zoning commission and the city council may amend the requirements of this chapter after giving public notice of any such proposed amendment and after holding a public hearing thereon as provided by crs  3123214   art ix 1986   2000 interpretation in the interpretation and application of the provisions of this chapter the following regulations shall govern 1 the provisions of this chapter shall be regarded as the minimum requirements for the protection of the public health safety comfort morals convenience prosperity and welfare this chapter shall therefore be regarded as remedial and shall be liberally construed to further its underlying purposes 2 whenever both a provision of this chapter and any other provisions of this chapter or any provision in any other law ordinance resolution rule or regulation of any kind contain any restrictions covering any of the same subject matter whichever restrictions are more restrictive or impose higher standards or requirements shall govern 3 this chapter is not intended to abrogate or annul a any permits issued before the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter was derived  or b any easement covenant or other private agreement   art x 1986   2000 taxation article i  in general definitions and meaning terms used in this chapter which are defined in crs title 39 art 26 shall have the same meaning as provided 1968   1993   2000   2001   2 2010   definitions in general a the following words terms and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning agricultural producer means a person regularly engaged in the business of using land for the production of commercial crops or commercial livestock the term agricultural producer includes farmers market gardeners commercial fruit growers livestock breeders dairy persons poultry persons and other persons similarly engaged but does not include a person who breeds or markets animals birds or fish for domestic pets nor a person who cultivates grows or harvests plants or plant products exclusively for that persons own consumption or casual sale aircraft means a device that is used or intended to be used for flight in the air aircraft part means any tangible personal property that is intended to be permanently affixed or attached as a component part of an aircraft aircraft simulator means a flight simulator training device fstd as defined in part 1 of title 14 of the federal regulations that is qualified in accordance with part 60 of title 14 of the federal regulations for use in a federal aviation administrationapproved flight training program aircraft simulator part means any tangible personal property that is originally designed and intended to be permanently affixed or attached as a component part of an aircraft and which will also function when it is permanently affixed or attached as a component part of an aircraft simulator airline company means any operator who engages in the carriage by aircraft of persons or property as a common carrier for compensation or hire or the carriage of mail or any aircraft operator who operates regularly between two or more points and publishes a flight schedule the term airline company shall not include operators whose aircraft are all certified for a gross takeoff weight of 12500 pounds or less and who do not engage in scheduled service or mail carriage service auction means any sale where tangible personal property is sold by an auctioneer who is either the agent for the owner of such property or is in fact the owner thereof automotive vehicle means any vehicle or device in upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a public highway or any device used or designed for aviation or flight in the air the term automotive vehicle includes but is not limited to motor vehicles trailers semitrailers or mobile homes the term automotive vehicle shall not include devices moved by human power or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks business means all activities engaged in or caused to be engaged in with the object of gain benefit or advantage either direct or indirect candy means a preparation of sugar honey or other natural or artificial sweeteners in combination with chocolate fruit nuts or other ingredients or flavorings in the form of bars drops or pieces the term candy does not include any preparation containing flour products that require refrigeration or marijuanainfused products carrier access services means the services furnished by a local exchange company to its customers who provide telecommunications services which allow them to provide such telecommunications services charitable organization means any entity which 1 has been certified as a nonprofit organization under c3 of the internal revenue   and 2 is an organization which exclusively and in a manner consistent with existing laws and for the benefit of an indefinite number of persons or animals freely and voluntarily ministers to the physical mental or spiritual needs of persons or animals and thereby lessens the burden of government coins means monetized bullion or other forms of money manufactured from gold silver platinum palladium or other such metals now in the future or heretofore designated as a medium of exchange under the laws of the state the united states or any foreign nation collection costs shall include but is not limited to all costs of audit assessment bank fees hearings monthly tax collected is less than $1000 to make returns and pay taxes at intervals no greater than every three months    1968 retailers with multiple locations a retailer doing business in two or    1968   2000 recovery of taxes penalties and interest a all sums of money paid by the purchaser to the vendor or retailer as taxes imposed by this article shall be and remain public money the property of the city in the hands of such vendor or retailer and he or she shall hold the same in trust for the sole use and benefit of the city until paid to the city clerk as herein provided  and for failure to pay the same to the city clerk such retailer shall be punished for a violation thereof b if any person neglects or refuses to make return and payment of the tax as required by this article the city clerk shall make an estimate based on such information as may be available of the amount of taxes due for the period for which the taxpayer is delinquent  and upon the basis of such estimated amount compute and assess in addition thereto a penalty equal to ten percent thereof together with interest on such delinquent taxes at the rate of one percent per month from the date when due promptly thereafter the city clerk shall give the delinquent taxpayer written notice of such estimated taxes penalty and interest which notice must be served personally or by certified mail such estimate shall thereupon become an assessment and such assessment shall be final and due and payable from the taxpayer to the city clerk ten days from the date of service of the notice or the date of mailing by certified mail  provided however that within said tenday period such delinquent taxpayer may petition the city clerk for a revision or modification of such assessment and shall within such tenday period furnish the city clerk with the facts and correct figures showing the correct amount of such taxes such petition shall be in writing and the facts and figures submitted shall be either in writing or orally and shall be given under the oath of said taxpayer thereupon the city clerk shall modify such assessment in accordance with the facts submitted which facts he or she deems correct such assessments shall be considered the final order of the city clerk and may be reviewed under rule 106a of the colorado rules of civil procedure as provided in this article c if any taxes penalty or interest imposed by this article and shown due by returns filed by the taxpayer or as shown by assessments duly made as provided herein are not paid within five days after the same are due the city clerk shall issue a notice setting forth the name of the taxpayer the amount of the tax penalties and interest the date of the accrual thereof and that the city claims a first and prior lien therefor on the real and tangible personal property of the taxpayer except as to preexisting claims or liens of a bona fide mortgagee pledgee judgment creditor or purchaser whose rights shall have attached prior to the filing of the notice as herein provided on property of the taxpayer other than goods stock in trade and business fixtures of such taxpayer said notice shall be on forms prepared by the city clerk and shall be verified by him or her or any duly qualified deputy or agent of the city clerk whose duties are the collection of such tax and may be filed in the office of the clerk and recorder of any county in the state in which the taxpayer owns real or tangible personal property the filing of such notice shall create such lien on such property in that county and constitute a notice thereof after said notice has been filed or concurrently therewith or at any time when taxes due are unpaid whether such notice is filed or not the city clerk may issue a warrant directed to any duly authorized revenue collector or to the sheriff of any county in the state commanding him or her to levy upon seize and sell sufficient of the real and personal property of the tax debtor found within his or her county for the payment of the amount due together with interest penalties and costs as now or hereafter provided by ordinance subject to valid preexisting claims or liens as above provided d such revenue collector or sheriff shall forthwith levy upon sufficient property of the taxpayer or any property used by such taxpayer in conducting his or her retail business and said property so levied upon shall be sold in all respects with like effect and in the same manner as is prescribed by law in respect to execution against property upon judgment of a court of record and the remedies of garnishments shall apply the sheriff shall be entitled to such fees in executing such warrant as are allowed by law for similar services e any liens for taxes as shown on the records of the county clerk and recorder as herein provided shall upon the payment of all taxes penalties and interest covered thereby be released by the city clerk in the same manner as mortgages or judgments are released f the city clerk may also treat any such taxes penalties or interest due and unpaid as a debt due the city from the vendor in case of failure to pay the tax or any portion thereof or any penalty or interest thereon when due the city clerk may recover at law the amount of such taxes penalties and interest in any justice county or district court of the county wherein the taxpayer resides or has his or her principal place of business having jurisdiction of the amount sought to be collected the return of the taxpayer or the assessments made by the city clerk as herein provided shall be prima facie proof of the amount due such actions may be actions in attachments and writs of attachment may be issued to the appropriate law enforcement officer in any such proceeding no bond shall be required of the city clerk nor shall any law enforcement officer require of the city clerk an indemnifying bond for executing the writ of attachment or writ of execution upon any judgment entered in such proceedings  and the city clerk may prosecute appeals or writs of error in such cases without the necessity of providing bond therefor it shall be the duty of the city attorney when requested by the city clerk to commence action for the recovery of taxes due under this article and the remedy shall be in addition to all other existing remedies or remedies provided in this article g in any action affecting the title to real estate or the ownership or rights to possession of personal property the city may be made a party defendant for the purpose of obtaining a interest imposed in excess of six percent per annum shall be deemed a penalty    1968   1993   2000   2006 intentional deficiency if any part of the deficiency is due to fraud with the intent to evade after written notice and demand by the city clerk and an additional one percent per month on said amount shall be added from the date the return was due until paid    1968 violations in addition no following conditions precedent applications for refund must be made within 60 days after the purchase of the goods whereon an exemption is claimed  must be supported by the affidavit of the purchaser accompanied by the original paid invoice or sales receipt and certificate issued by the seller  and must be made upon such forms as shall be prescribed and formulated by the city clerk which forms refund must be made by the same person who purchased the goods and paid the tax thereon as shown in the invoice of the sale thereof no applicant for refund under the provisions of this article or any other person shall make any false statement in connection with an application for a refund of any taxes b should a dispute arise between the purchaser and seller as to whether or not any sale is exempt from taxation hereunder the seller shall nevertheless collect and the purchaser shall pay such tax and the seller shall thereupon issue to the purchaser a receipt or certificate on forms prescribed by the city clerk showing the names of the seller and purchaser the items purchased the date price amount of tax paid and a brief statement of the claim of exemption the purchaser the city clerk shall then cooperate with other participating municipalities in the development of arrangements for the coordinated audit including arrangement of the time during which the coordinated participating municipalities to whenever practicable minimize the number of auditors who will be present on the taxpayers premises to conduct the coordinated audit on behalf of the participating municipalities information obtained by or on behalf of those municipalities participating in the coordinated audit may be shared only among such participating municipalities f if the taxpayers request section    1993   2000 intercity claims for recovery a the intent of this article is to streamline and standardize procedures related to situations where tax has been remitted to the incorrect municipality it is not intended to reduce or eliminate the responsibilities of the taxpayer or vendor to correctly pay collect and remit sales and use taxes to the city b as used herein the term claim for recovery means a claim for reimbursement of sales and use taxes paid to the wrong taxing jurisdiction c when it is determined by the city clerk that sales and use tax owed to the city has been reported and paid to another municipality the city shall promptly notify the vendor that taxes are being improperly collected and remitted and that as of the date of the notice the vendor must cease improper tax collections and remittances d the city may make a written claim for recovery directly to the municipality that received tax andor penalty and interest owed to the city or in the alternative may institute procedures for collection of the tax from the taxpayer or vendor the decision to make a claim for recovery lies in the sole discretion of the city any claim for recovery shall include a properly executed release of claim from the taxpayer andor vendor releasing its claim to the taxes paid to the wrong municipality evidence to substantiate the claim and a request that the municipality approve or deny in whole or in part the claim within 90 days of its receipt the municipality to which the city submits a claim for recovery may for good cause request an extension of time to investigate the claim and approval of such extension by the city shall not be unreasonably withheld e the city may deny a claim on the grounds that it has previously paid a claim for recovery arising out of an audit of the same taxpayer f the period subject to a claim for recovery shall be limited to the 36month period prior to the date the municipality that was wrongly paid the tax receives the claim for recovery    1993 notice of sales and use tax ordinance amendment a in order to initiate a central register of sales and use tax ordinances for municipalities that administer 2007 utilities article i  in general secs 2812818  reserved article ii  water and sewer service division 1  generally water conservation a the public works department is hereby directed to at all times closely and diligently monitor the water supply available to the municipal water system to inform the city council and the water advisory board on a timely basis as to the condition and circumstances of the thenavailable water supply and to take such measures as the department may deem necessary to educate and inform the public as to the need for conservation of the city water supply and methods whereby said water supply might be conserved and to investigate all measures aimed toward preserving the integrity of the municipal water system b in the discretion of the city council in consultation with the public works department and the water advisory board and as water availability and quality circumstances might dictate the city council is hereby authorized and directed to implement voluntary water conservation restrictions on the use of water for some or all purposes by some or all users of the municipal water system said voluntary conservation restrictions shall be as set forth by resolution adopted by the city council    2 1989   2000   water use restrictions a mandatory water use restrictions shall be considered for implementation at any time the following criteria are met 1 an emergency occurs as determined by the public works director in consultation with the city administrator which disrupts the citys ability to distribute water water distribution system  or 2 water availability and quality conditions as determined by the public works director in consultation with the city administrator and the water advisory board dictate the need for mandatory water use restrictions b in the event that the criteria for mandatory water use restrictions described in subsection a of this section shall be disclosed to the city council by the public works director and city administrator the city council as water availability and quality circumstances might dictate is hereby authorized to implement mandatory water use restrictions on the use of water for some or all purposes by some or all users of the municipal water system said mandatory water use restrictions shall be as set forth by resolution adopted by the city council by a phone poll or an inperson majority vote    1989   2000   emergency restrictions nothing herein contained shall be construed or interpreted as limiting or prohibiting the imposition of water use restrictions more stringent than as described above provided that such further restrictions shall be implemented if at all by the city council in emergency circumstances    1989 unauthorized tapping and usage govern the provisions of all water and sewer services furnished by the city whether inside or outside the city limits b any applicant or developer seeking to obtain city water and sewer services or any other city services exclusive of electrical service to premises outside of the city shall be required as a condition precedent to the furnishing of such services to execute and deliver agreements governing the usage of said extraterritorial premises including but not limited to agreements requiring annexation agreements concerning water restrictions and agreements in respect of the citys zoning and subdivision ordinances including but not limited to street lighting plans traffic regulatory sign plans street names sign plans stormwater system plans and street system layouts and plans for the purpose of street extension alignment orderly growth and traffic flow  and finally all applicable building and construction codes of the city such as but not limited to building code building code standards fire code fire code standards mechanical code housing code plumbing code and the code for abatement of dangerous buildings no water sewer or other city services excepting electrical service shall be extended to serve any building development or subdivision outside of the citys corporate limits without such agreements as may be required and without satisfactory guaranty to the city of the ability to comply with the requirements of said agreements said agreements shall be binding upon the applicant or developer his or her heirs successors administrators and assigns and shall be considered as covenants running with the land thus developed c applicants or developers shall be required to grant and convey to the city all necessary rightsofway and easements for installation and maintenance of city utility lines all lines and equipment necessary for the furnishing of extraterritorial water and sewer services with the exception of service lines shall be conveyed to the city d all installations of extraterritorial water and sewer service shall be performed at the cost of the applicant or developer with all fees including tap fees to be paid in advance of the issuance of connection all connections shall be inspected by the building official or by appropriate city personnel with the applicant or developer to pay any costs incurred all such water and wastewater taps shall be restricted exclusively to the site designated in the application fees and costs incurred by the applicant or developer are not refundable and the applicant or owner shall be required to furnish appropriate performance construction or other types of bonding as may be required by the city to protect its interest at the citys discretion appropriate escrow arrangements may be substituted in lieu of required bonding e the minimum size of any water main shall be six inches the city reserves the right to establish type size location and all other specifications regarding water mains sewer trunk lines valves and other necessary equipment all water mains shall be looped in accordance with state health department regulations and city requirements water mains shall be sufficient to provide for fire protection with fire hydrants to be installed by city personnel at the expense of the applicant or developer f the city shall determine in its sole discretion the number of taps to be provided along with location and size depending upon capacity and water availability use restrictions may be implemented by the city council at its discretion and by the public works department in the event of emergencies nothing in this article or rising out of the citys provisions of extraterritorial water and sewer services shall operate to transform the city into a public utility it being fully understood that the city is not a public utility but is a municipallyoperated water and sewer system with citizens of the city having first and prior privilege to draw upon the citys water and sewer installations g in appropriate circumstances and at the sole discretion of the city council water districts may be formed in which cases master meters shall be installed by city personnel with the cost incurred being borne by the applicant or developer said master meters shall be owned and maintained by the city and such districts shall be governed by such agreements as may be entered into between such districts and the city council mergers and dissolutions of existing city districts shall be reviewed and adopted by agreement between the applicant or owner and the city council h any agreement for the provision of extraterritorial water and sewer services by the city shall include penalty provisions for noncompliance by the applicant or owner of any part of any agreement entered into pursuant to this section or for any violation of this section any such agreement shall further provide provisions regarding main extension or reimbursement whereby the owner or developer shall be enabled to recover a reasonable portion of the expenses incurred in the process of installing water or sewer services but the city retains the right to refuse permission for any extension or expansion of extraterritorial water or sewer services i upon proper application the water advisory board may consider application for waiver of any of the provisions hereinabove set forth and may forward to the city council a recommendation for such waiver to be granted in respect of any of the provisions of this section wherein waiver might be deemed appropriate such recommendation by the water advisory board is recommendatory only and shall not be binding upon the city council the city reserves the right to require recordation of all or any portion of any agreement entered into in respect of this section      1996   2000 connection to sewage system required no person shall construct or maintain a privy vault or toilet unconnected with the sewage system of the city or a cesspool on any lot or parcel of land where such lot or parcel of land is so situated that it can be connected with the city sewage system except when the city shall find that such connection cannot be made prior      sewer connections the city shall make the tap for connection into the main with materials furnished by the property owner or person making the connection and no connection shall be made by any person other than in this manner the lines from the main to the property line shall be vitrified clay or its equal and shall be joined together by gk material or equal each connection shall be four inches or larger in size all connections shall be made to the satisfaction of the city including refilling and replacing of dirt removed to make such connection prior          1989   2000 water meters a all persons obtaining water from the city shall have such water supplied only water meter separate meters shall be required for each consumer b no water meter in excess of one inch shall be furnished installed or connected to any water main of the city to furnish water to any property used for residential purposes provided that hotels and motels shall not be considered residential purposes consumers other than residential shall be entitled to meters in excess of one inch provided that all the provisions of this article applicable to such meters are followed c when any water meter in excess of one inch used to measure water to property used for residential purposes shall be disconnected for seasonal purposes or otherwise the same shall be replaced only by a oneinch meter or less d notwithstanding any other provision of this article any water consumer may apply for and have any noncomplying water meter exchanged for any smaller size meter which complies with this article without any charge for connection disconnection or differential in meter sizes e any water consumer entitled to the installation of a meter in excess of threequarters of an inch shall pay to the city prior to the installation and connection of such meter a sum equal to the difference in cost to the city between a threequarterinch meter and the size meter desired such cost shall be the cost at the time of application of the installation of such meter f there shall be assessed and collected by the city a reconnection charge as established by the city council to reconnect any meter which has been disconnected for seasonal purposes or otherwise g if any water meter shall fail to register during any given month the consumer chargeable for such meter shall be charged for use of water for such month a sum equal to the average charge for consumption as shown by such meter when in order for a period of 12 months prior to such month prior 8         2000 secs 28542879  reserved division 3  fees and constitute a lien upon the real estate to which the water is furnished and shall constitute a charge against the owner thereof if for any cause any such charges shall become delinquent the water supply for such real estate shall be cut off by the city and in no case shall it be turned on to the same real estate until all such delinquencies have been paid in full together with interest at the rate of five percent per annum plus a charge as established by the city council no change of ownership or occupation of such real estate shall bar the application of this section b in addition to the remedies for delinquent water bills set out in this article the city clerk when ordered by the city council shall cause any delinquent charges for the use of water to be certified to the county clerk footnotes  1  state law reference water activities enterprises crs  37451101 et seq water enterprise a there is hereby established pursuant to the terms and provisions of the water activity law crs  37451101 the city of lamar water activity enterprise the enterprise the enterprise shall consist of the business represented by all of the citys water and sewer facilities and properties now owned or hereafter acquired whether situated within or outside the city boundaries including all present or future improvements extensions enlargements betterments replacements or additions thereof or thereto the system the enterprise shall have all of the authority powers rights obligations and duties as may be provided or permitted by the water activity law and the state constitution and as may be further prescribed by ordinance or resolution of the city b the governing body of the enterprise shall be the city council and shall be subject to all of the applicable laws rules and regulations pertaining to the city council whenever the city council is in session the governing body shall also be deemed to be in session it shall not be necessary for the governing body to meet separately from the regular and special meetings of the city council nor shall it be necessary for the governing body to specifically announce or acknowledge that actions taken thereby are taken by the governing body of the enterprise the governing body may conduct its affairs in the same manner and subject to the same laws which apply to the city council for the same or similar matters provided that in accordance with crs  374511042 the governing body may authorize the issuance of bonds by adoption of a resolution provided that all provisions of the home rule charter shall be complied with c the enterprise shall at all times and in all ways conduct its affairs so as to continue to qualify as a water activity enterprise within the meaning of crs  37451102 and as an enterprise within the meaning of article x section 20 of the state constitution specifically but not by way of limitation the enterprise is not authorized to and shall not receive ten percent or more of its annual revenue in grants from all state and local governments combined d the enterprise is authorized to issue bonds notes or other obligations payable from the revenues derived or to be derived from the system in accordance with the water activity law the city council may also authorize the issuance of such bonds notes or other obligations in accordance with applicable state laws and the citys home rule charter and in so doing shall be deemed to be acting as the governing body    1998   2000 secs 2812128138  reserved article iii  franchises division 1  generally renewal of franchises all members of the city staff are hereby directed and authorized to become informed and knowledgeable regarding the terms conditions and pertinent facts in relation to the public utility franchises granted by the city and to do and perform all things necessary to cause renewal or replacement franchises in respect of said public utilities to be accomplished so as to avoid any cessation of the services provided by such public utilities    1995 continuation of franchise in the event that any such public utility franchise expires without previous and timely renewal or replacement thereof being accomplished such public utility provider whose franchise has thus expired and which shall continue to function and provide public utility service to the inhabitants of the city shall be and hereby is deemed to be providing such services and continuing to function and conduct its business pursuant to a revocable business permit as described in section 1210 of the home rule charter    1995 conditions for continuation all conditions agreements limitations rights privileges and duties of any such continuing public utility service provider except the term and duration of such arrangement shall continue on the identical basis and arrangement for which the original franchise of such public utility provided and particularly being the fee or compensation originally agreed upon in the franchise of such public utility service provider as mandated to be paid to the city pursuant to section 126 of the home rule charter    1995 duration of continuation the term and duration of the continuing business permit afforded to such public utility service provider herein shall be for such time as is reasonably necessary in order to negotiate for a renewal of such franchise and obtain voter approval thereof to allow such public utility service provider to close out its business or to allow such public utility service provider to dispose of or remove its property from the city during any such continuation of public utilities pursuant to the business permit arrangements hereinabove set forth neither the city nor the public utility service provider shall have the right to terminate such permit sooner than 180 days after giving written notice to the opposite party of its intentions so to terminate    1995   2000 access to city property a the continuation of any public utility service by a provider pursuant to the business permit arrangement hereinabove set forth shall not be deemed to be a trespass by the public utility service provider upon city property b no such continuation of public utility service pursuant to the business permit arrangement shall be deemed to be a renewal of any such franchise nor shall the same be deemed to be a grant of such franchise the same being instead an implied consent to use of municipal property upon previously agreed upon conditions for an indefinite but limited period of time in the best interest of all citizens of the city    6 1995 approval of voters nothing the present and future streets and alleys of the city its mains pipes boxes reducing and regulating stations laterals conduits and service extensions together with all of the necessary appurtenances for the purpose of supplying natural gas for light heat power and other purposes to the city and the inhabitants thereof and users therein including domestic commercial public authority and industrial consumers for the term of this franchise subject however to the limitations herein set forth and provided provisions applicable to the furnishing of natural gas to the city light plant by the company shall be set forth in a separate contract    1995   2000 term a the rights privileges and franchise herein granted to and conferred upon the company shall extend for a term of ten years from  until the tuesday after the first monday in november 200 and for an extended period of ten years which may thereafter be granted as hereinafter set forth b after  and before  the company shall file with the city a report that documents the efforts and progress that the company has made in meeting the citys objectives of ensuring safe reliable and bestcost natural gas service for and to natural gas consumers within the city upon receipt of the report the city shall conduct an inquiry into the facts presented and will determine city council whether the company should be granted the hereinabove referenced tenyear extension of the franchise which grant shall not be unreasonably withheld    1995 effective date the effective date for the grant of franchise shall be  pursuant to section 125 of the city home rule charter the company shall be liable for its proportionate cost and expense of said election    1995   2000 compensation a for this grant and as consideration for use and occupancy of the streets alleys and public grounds the company shall pay monthly on the volumes consumed commencing  five percent of the gross revenue realized from the sales of gas for domestic commercial and industrial use in the city provided that the franchise fee provided for in this article shall not be charged or collected for gas used by any governmental unit or taxexempt organization which has provided the company with written notification of its status b for the purpose of ascertaining or auditing the correct amount to be paid under the provisions of this article the city shall have reasonable access to the appropriate books of the company for the purpose of checking the gross income received from operations within the city the company shall not be required to generate books and records which it does not maintain in its regular course of business c it is understood that payment of such franchise charge does not excuse the company from payment of either sales and use taxes or property taxes as such taxes are levied from time to time    1995   2000 laying pipe a the company shall use its best efforts to lay all new construction pipeline at least 24 inches below the surface of the streets alleys and avenues at least such depth below the bottom of all drain ditches and in a manner which does not interfere with any present public or private drains sewers water mains sidewalks paving or other public improvements the city reserves the right to construct change or repair any public improvements and to change the grades of any street avenue or alley should the same be changed constructed or repaired the company is required at its own expense to lower change or alter the pipelines to harmonize the regulations herein and not to interfere with the conduits water lines sewers sidewalks paving drains or other public improvements of the city or the public utilities of the city the company agrees to perform routine maintenance and surveillance in accordance with industry standards to ensure that pipeline depth complies with applicable state codes and regulations b if practicable no pipeline shall be laid closer than two feet from any water main or other pipe or conduit of other utilities    1995   2000 repairs and replacements all earth materials sidewalks pavings crossings or improvements of any kind required or removed by the company shall be fully or property on account of the construction installation operation and maintenance of said distribution system unless such loss or damage occurs as a result of the negligence of the city or its citizens    1995 excavations supervised an excavation by the company in any of the streets alleys avenues roads or public grounds within the limits of the city shall be done in accordance with such served or upon easements of rightsofway adjacent thereto company employees or agents shall have the right to enter upon such consumers premises and read or inspect its meters at reasonable times during daylight hours the company shall furnish reliable gas meters as described in section 28181    1995 standards for natural gas supply the company shall maintain and operate its plants and system and render efficient service in accordance with the rules and regulations of the puc and the terms and conditions of this article including specifically but without limitation the following requirements 1 heating value natural gas sold supplied and delivered under this franchise shall be maintained at a monthly average of not less than 950 british thermal units of heat value per cubic foot a cubic foot of gas means that amount of gas which when saturated with water vapor at a temperature of 60 degrees fahrenheit and subject to an absolute pressure equal to 30 inches of mercury at 32 degrees fahrenheit 1473 pounds per square inch occupies a volume of one cubic foot gas sold under this franchise shall be accurately measured utilizing equipment of a type approved or allowed by the puc upon the citys request the company will provide the city with copies of any calorimeter and pressure reports that it maintains 2 natural gas natural gas may be furnished to the city from wells pipelines or gas processing plants and the company shall remove any objectionable constituents or noxious gases therefrom and add such odorizing agent as may be required by law or regulations of any applicable regulatory authority 3 pressure of service until and unless lawfully changed the standard of pressure of service shall be the same as now or hereafter approved by or acceptable to the puc 4 maintenance of system the company shall maintain its gas plant equipment and distribution system in good condition and repair at all times    1995   2000 rates and conditions of service the rates to be charged and exacted from the city and its inhabitants and the rules and regulations with reference to the character quality and standards of service to be furnished by the company shall be under the jurisdiction and control of the puc or such regulatory body as may from time to time during this grant be vested by law with authority and jurisdiction of the rates regulations and quality and standards of service to be supplied by the company  provided however that nothing contained within this section shall be construed or interpreted as obviating the necessity for the company to receive discrimination or preference prohibited a the company shall not as to rates or service make or grant any unreasonable preference or advantage to any consumer or subject any consumer to any schedules to which any consumer coming within an established classification would be entitled b the rates to be charged by the company for industrial gas used in the city may be lower and different correct such condition the city may declare this franchise forfeited and terminated in which event the company shall as provided in division 1 of this article continue to render service as theretofore   1995 failure of gas supply during the term of the franchise should there occur a failure or partial failure of the supply of natural gas available to the company because of depletion of such supply the company shall take all reasonable steps to obtain an additional natural gas supply from other sources to be delivered to the company and if unable to procure the same it is hereby authorized to supply artificial or mixed gas for the unexpired term of this franchise if the company within a reasonable period after failure of the supply of natural gas shall fail to supply to its customers artificial andor mixed gas the franchise rights granted herein shall terminate    1995 changing conditions the city and the company recognize that the gas industry is currently the subject of discussion examination and inquiry by different segments of the industry and by state and federal regulators and that these activities may ultimately result in fundamental changes in the way the company conducts its business and meets its service obligations therefore at the request of either party the city and the company agree to meet with each other and discuss in good faith amendments to the franchise to reflect a proper accommodation of such developments    1995 local office maintained the company shall during the life of the franchise maintain an adequately staffed service and management office within the city    1995 zoning article i  in general definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning accessory building means a subordinate building or portion of the main building the use of which customarily is incidental to that of the main building or to the main use of the premises for the purposes of this chapter the term accessory building shall include dish antennas and similar structures accessory use means a subordinate purpose for which the land or structures thereon are designed or intended alley means a public thoroughfare which provides only a secondary means of access to abutting property the rightofway of which is 20 feet or less in width alter means any structural change in the supporting or loadbearing members of a building such as bearing walls columns beams girders or floor joists animal hospital or clinic means an establishment where animals are admitted principally for examination treatment board or care by a doctor of veterinary medicine this does not include open kennels or runs apartment see dwelling multiple family aquaculture means the science and endeavor of producing and raising on a commercial basis fish or shellfish in confined tanks or beds of water basement person other than residents of the premises shall be engaged in such occupation  b the occupation is customarily incidental to the use of the premises as a dwelling place  c not more than one nonilluminated nameplate is used  d the nameplate shall be attached to the building and shall not exceed one square foot in area  e the occupation does not occupy more than 25 percent of the floor area of one floor of the principal building when such use is carried on in the principal building  f no display will indicate from the exterior of the building that the premises are being used in part for any purpose other than a dwelling  g there is no commodity displayed or stored on the premises except that which is prepared on the premises  h no equipment or process shall be used in such home occupation which creates noise vibration glare fumes odors or electrical interference detectable to the normal senses of a person off the lot if the occupation is conducted in a singlefamily residence or outside the individual dwelling unit if conducted in other than a singlefamily residence in the case of electrical interference no equipment or process shall be used which creates visual or audible interference in any radio or television receivers off the premises or causes fluctuations in line voltage off the premises  and i no traffic shall be generated by such home occupation in greater volumes than would normally be expected in a residential neighborhood 2 the term home occupation does not include the growth or cultivation of marijuana for medical purposes and a medical marijuana center may not be operated as a home occupation hospital means an establishment used primarily for inpatient care and provision of health medical mental and surgical care of the sick or injured distance between the midpoints of straight lines connecting the foremost points of the side lot lines in the front and the rearmost points of the side lot lines in the rear 2 width of a lot is between side lot lines at their foremost points where they intersect with the street line shall not be less than 80 percent of the required lot width except in the case of lots on the turning circle
